					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">United Nations</span></h1>
							
<div id="p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown mw-portlet mw-portlet-lang"  >
	<input type="checkbox" id="p-lang-btn-checkbox" role="button" aria-haspopup="true" data-event-name="ui.dropdown-p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown-checkbox mw-interlanguage-selector" aria-label="Go to an article in another language. Available in 293 languages"   >
	<label id="p-lang-btn-label" for="p-lang-btn-checkbox" class="vector-dropdown-label cdx-button cdx-button--fake-button cdx-button--fake-button--enabled cdx-button--weight-quiet cdx-button--action-progressive mw-portlet-lang-heading-293" aria-hidden="true"  ><span class="vector-icon mw-ui-icon-language-progressive mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-language-progressive"></span>

<span class="vector-dropdown-label-text">293 languages</span>
	</label>
	<div class="vector-dropdown-content">

		<div class="vector-menu-content">
			
			<ul class="vector-menu-content-list">

<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="font-size: 102%;;color: var(--color-base)">Activities</div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content" style="font-size: 102%;"><a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations peacekeeping</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Nations_peacekeeping_missions" title="List of United Nations peacekeeping missions">missions</a>)&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_territories_administered_by_the_United_Nations" title="List of territories administered by the United Nations">governed territories</a>)&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Police" title="United Nations Police">UNPOL</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Rights_of_Indigenous_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Rights of Indigenous Peoples">UNDRIP</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Convention" title="World Heritage Convention">World Heritage Convention</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b>&#32;<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Declaration_on_the_Rights_of_Peasants" title="United Nations Declaration on the Rights of Peasants">Declaration on the Rights of Peasants</a></div></div></td>

<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_resolution" title="United Nations resolution">Resolutions</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239400231">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}}@media print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:United_Nations_series" title="Template:United Nations series"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:United_Nations_series" title="Template talk:United Nations series"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:United_Nations_series" title="Special:EditPage/Template:United Nations series"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239400231" /><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Extraterritorialities" title="Template:Extraterritorialities"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Extraterritorialities" title="Template talk:Extraterritorialities"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Extraterritorialities" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Extraterritorialities"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>United Nations</b> (<b>UN</b>) is a global <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a> established by the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">UN Charter</a> on 26 June 1945 with the articulated mission of maintaining <a href="/wiki/International_peace" class="mw-redirect" title="International peace">international peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_security" title="International security">security</a>, to develop friendly <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">relations</a> among <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">states</a>, to promote international cooperation, and to serve as a centre for harmonizing the actions of states in achieving those goals.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_headquarters" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations headquarters">United Nations headquarters</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, with several other offices located in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Nairobi" title="United Nations Office at Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Vienna" title="United Nations Office at Vienna">Vienna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. The UN comprises six principal organizations: the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">Secretariat</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a> which, together with several <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies</a> and related agencies, make up the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a>. There are in total 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>, representing nearly all of the world's <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>, as well as two <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">observer states</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">Palestine</a>. 
</p><p>The UN has primarily focused on economic and social development, particularly during the wave of <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> in the mid-20th century. The UN currently operates <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">11 peacekeeping missions</a>, by order of inception, in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Truce_Supervision_Organization" title="United Nations Truce Supervision Organization">the Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/UN_mediation_of_the_Kashmir_dispute" title="UN mediation of the Kashmir dispute">Kashmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Force_in_Cyprus" title="United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Disengagement_Observer_Force" title="United Nations Disengagement Observer Force">Golan Heights</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_for_the_Referendum_in_Western_Sahara" title="United Nations Mission for the Referendum in Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/MONUSCO" title="MONUSCO">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Security_Force_for_Abyei" title="United Nations Interim Security Force for Abyei">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_South_Sudan" title="United Nations Mission in South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/MINUSCA" title="MINUSCA">Central African Republic</a>. The UN has been recognized as a leader of peace and human development, with many officers and agencies having been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, but has also been <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_United_Nations" title="Criticism of the United Nations">criticized for perceived ineffectiveness, bias, and corruption</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Nations" title="History of the United Nations">History of the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Background_(pre-1941)"><span id="Background_.28pre-1941.29"></span>Background (pre-1941)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Haile_Selassie_League_of_Nations_speech.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Emperor_Haile_Selassie_League_of_Nations_speech.png/250px-Emperor_Haile_Selassie_League_of_Nations_speech.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="182" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Emperor_Haile_Selassie_League_of_Nations_speech.png/500px-Emperor_Haile_Selassie_League_of_Nations_speech.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1099" data-file-height="799" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie I</a> at the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> appealing Italy's 1936 invasion in which the League failed to intervene.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the century prior to the UN's creation, several <a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organizations</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> were formed to ensure protection and assistance for victims of armed conflict and strife.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, several major leaders, especially <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. president</a> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Woodrow_Wilson_administration" title="Foreign policy of the Woodrow Wilson administration">Woodrow Wilson</a>, advocated for a world body to guarantee peace. The winners of the war, the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>, met to decide on formal peace terms at the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference_(1919%E2%80%931920)" title="Paris Peace Conference (1919–1920)">Paris Peace Conference</a>. The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was approved and started operations, but the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> never joined. On 10 January 1920, the League of Nations formally came into being when the <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations" title="Covenant of the League of Nations">Covenant of the League of Nations</a>, ratified by 42 nations in 1919, took effect.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The League Council acted as an executive body directing the Assembly's business. It began with four permanent members—the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.
</p><p>After some limited successes and failures during the 1920s, the League proved ineffective in the 1930s, as it failed to act against the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Japanese invasion of Manchuria</a> in 1933.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Forty nations voted for Japan to withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> but Japan voted against it and walked out of the League instead of withdrawing from Manchuria.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also failed to act against the <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Second Italo-Ethiopian War</a>, after the appeal for international intervention by <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethiopian Emperor">Ethiopian Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie I</a> at Geneva in 1936 went with no avail, including when calls for economic sanctions against Italy failed. Italy and other nations left the League.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> broke out in 1939, the League effectively closed down.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Declarations_by_the_Allies_of_World_War_II_(1941–1944)"><span id="Declarations_by_the_Allies_of_World_War_II_.281941.E2.80.931944.29"></span>Declarations by the Allies of World War II (1941–1944)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg/250px-United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="288" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg/500px-United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="1659" /></a><figcaption>1943 sketch by Franklin Roosevelt of the UN original three branches: The <a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Policemen</a>, an executive branch, and an international assembly of forty UN member states.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The first step towards the establishment of the United Nations was the Inter-Allied Conference in London that led to the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_St_James%27s_Palace" title="Declaration of St James&#39;s Palace">Declaration of St James's Palace</a> on 12 June 1941.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By August 1941, American president <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin Roosevelt</a> and British prime minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> had drafted the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>; which defined goals for the post-war world. At the subsequent meeting of the Inter-Allied Council in London on 24 September 1941, the eight <a href="/wiki/List_of_governments_in_exile_during_World_War_II" title="List of governments in exile during World War II">governments in exile of countries under Axis occupation</a>, together with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French Forces">Free French Forces</a>, unanimously adopted adherence to the common principles of policy set forth by Britain and the United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt and Churchill met at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in December 1941 for the <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_Conference" title="Arcadia Conference">Arcadia Conference</a>. Roosevelt is considered a founder of the UN,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and coined the term <i>United Nations</i> to describe the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied countries</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Churchill accepted it, noting its use by <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The text of the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a> was drafted on 29 December 1941, by Roosevelt, Churchill, and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Hopkins" title="Harry Hopkins">Harry Hopkins</a>. It incorporated Soviet suggestions but included no role for France. One major change from the Atlantic Charter was the addition of a provision for <a href="/wiki/Religious_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious freedom">religious freedom</a>, which Stalin approved after Roosevelt insisted.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESherwood1948447–453&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherwood1948447–453-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt's idea of the "<a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Powers</a>", refers to the four major Allied countries, the United States, the United Kingdom, the Soviet Union, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">China</a>, emerged in the Declaration by the United Nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sheriff&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheriff-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On New Year's Day 1942, Roosevelt, Churchill, the Soviet Union's former Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov" title="Maxim Litvinov">Maxim Litvinov</a>, and the Chinese Premier <a href="/wiki/T._V._Soong" title="T. V. Soong">T. V. Soong</a> signed the "<a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a>",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the next day the representatives of twenty-two other nations added their signatures. During the war, the United Nations became the official term for the Allies. In order to join, countries had to sign the Declaration and declare war on the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2003&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2003-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The October 1943 <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conference_(1943)" title="Moscow Conference (1943)">Moscow Conference</a> resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Declarations" title="Moscow Declarations">Moscow Declarations</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Four_Nations" title="Declaration of the Four Nations">Four Power Declaration on General Security</a>. This declaration was signed by the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four (World War II)">Allied Big Four</a>—the United States, the Soviet Union, the United Kingdom, and China—and aimed for the creation "at the earliest possible date of a general international organization". This was the first public announcement that a new international organization was being contemplated to replace the League of Nations. The <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a> followed shortly afterwards at which Roosevelt, Churchill and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, the leader of the Soviet Union, met and discussed the idea of a post-war international organization.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The new international organization was formulated and negotiated amongst the delegations from the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four (World War II)">Allied Big Four</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Dumbarton_Oaks_Conference" title="Dumbarton Oaks Conference">Dumbarton Oaks Conference</a> from 21 September to 7 October 1944. They agreed on proposals for the aims, structure and functioning of the new organization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bohlen&#95;1973&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bohlen_1973-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It took the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">conference at Yalta</a> in February 1945, and further negotiations with the Soviet Union, before all the issues were resolved.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bohlen&#95;1973&#95;23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bohlen_1973-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Founding_(1945)"><span id="Founding_.281945.29"></span>Founding (1945)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png/500px-United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="195" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png/960px-United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1450" data-file-height="628" /></a><figcaption>The UN in 1945: founding members in light blue, protectorates and territories of the founding members in dark blue (Some nations' land would be different from now.)</figcaption></figure>
<p>By 1 March 1945, 21 additional states had signed the Declaration by the United Nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEOsmańczyk20042445&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOsmańczyk20042445-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After months of planning, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">UN Conference on International Organization</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> on 25 April 1945. It was attended by 50 nations' governments and a number of non-governmental organizations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Charter&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-UNHistory&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHistory-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The delegations of the Big Four chaired the plenary meetings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Previously, Churchill had urged Roosevelt to restore France to its status of a major power after the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Paris" title="Liberation of Paris">liberation of Paris</a> in August 1944. The drafting of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a> was completed over the following two months, and it was signed on 26 June 1945 by the representatives of the 50 countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN officially came into existence at 20:07 (<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>) on 24 October 1945,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> upon ratification of the Charter by the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>: the United States, the United Kingdom, France, the Soviet Union and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">China</a> — and by a majority of the other 46 nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1941to1950&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-original&#95;draft&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-original_draft-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_session_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="First session of the United Nations General Assembly">first meetings</a> of the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="General Assembly">General Assembly</a>, with 51 nations represented,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>b<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Security Council took place in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> beginning in January 1946.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1941to1950&#95;35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Debates began at once, covering topical issues such as the presence of Russian troops in <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian Azerbaijan">Iranian Azerbaijan</a> and British forces in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> British diplomat <a href="/wiki/Gladwyn_Jebb" title="Gladwyn Jebb">Gladwyn Jebb</a> served as interim secretary-general.
</p><p>The General Assembly selected <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> as the site for the headquarters of the UN. Construction began on 14 September 1948 and the facility was completed on 9 October 1952. The Norwegian Foreign Minister, <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a>, was the first elected <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN secretary-general</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1941to1950&#95;35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cold_War_(1947–1991)"><span id="Cold_War_.281947.E2.80.931991.29"></span>Cold War (1947–1991)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_(3x4_cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="253" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg/330px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg/500px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld_%283x4_cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2122" data-file-height="2825" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a> was a particularly active secretary-general from 1953 until he died in 1961.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Though the UN's primary mandate was <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>, the division between the United States and the Soviet Union often paralysed the organization; generally allowing it to intervene only in conflicts distant from the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199535&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199535-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two notable exceptions were a Security Council resolution on 7 July 1950 authorizing a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Command" title="United Nations Command">US-led coalition</a> to repel the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">North Korean invasion of South Korea</a>, passed in the absence of the Soviet Union,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1941to1950&#95;35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199558–59&#95;42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199558–59-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement" title="Korean Armistice Agreement">Korean Armistice Agreement</a> on 27 July 1953.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 November 1947, the General Assembly approved <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">Resolution 181</a>, a proposal to partition British Mandatory <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a> into two states, a Jewish state and an Arab state, with Jerusalem placed under international status.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Partition plan passed 33–13 with 10 abstentions and one absent. The plan was accepted by the Jews and rejected by the Arabs of Palestine and the Arab states <sup id="cite&#95;ref-186-20240719&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186-20240719-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> leading to <a href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine" title="1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine">civil war</a>. Following the declaration of the State of Israel on 15 May 1948, the surrounding Arab armies <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.nytimes.com/www.nytimes.com/learning/aol/onthisday/big/0514.html">invaded</a> Palestine, beginning the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab–Israeli War</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two years later, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bunche" title="Ralph Bunche">Ralph Bunche</a>, a UN official, negotiated <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">an armistice</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestine_war" title="1948 Palestine war">resulting conflict</a>, with the Security Council deciding that "an armistice shall be established in all sectors of Palestine".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-186-20240719&#95;45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186-20240719-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199551–54&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199551–54-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 7 November 1956, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force" title="United Nations Emergency Force">first UN peacekeeping force</a> was established to end the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1951to1960&#95;48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1951to1960-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> however, the UN was unable to intervene against the Soviet Union's simultaneous invasion of <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, following <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">the country's revolution</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995114&#95;49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995114-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 July 1960, the UN established the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_the_Congo" title="United Nations Operation in the Congo">United Nations Operation in the Congo</a> (or UNOC), the largest military force of its early decades, to bring order to <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katanga</a>, restoring it to the control of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> by 11 May 1964.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995115–134&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995115–134-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While travelling to meet rebel leader <a href="/wiki/Moise_Tshombe" class="mw-redirect" title="Moise Tshombe">Moise Tshombe</a> during the conflict, <a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a>, often named as one of the UN's most effective secretaries-general,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199576&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199576-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200760&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200760-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200417,&#95;20&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200417,_20-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1961_Ndola_United_Nations_DC-6_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="1961 Ndola United Nations DC-6 crash">died in a plane crash</a>. Months later he was posthumously awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995127–128,&#95;134&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995127–128,_134-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1964, Hammarskjöld's successor, <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a>, deployed the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Force_in_Cyprus" title="United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus">UN Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus</a>, which would become one of the UN's longest-running peacekeeping missions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995156–157&#95;55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995156–157-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With the spread of <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> in the 1960s, the UN's membership shot up due to an influx of newly independent nations. In 1960 alone, 17 new states joined the UN, 16 of them from Africa.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1951to1960&#95;48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1951to1960-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 25 October 1971, with opposition from the United States, but with the support of many <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a> nations, the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> was given the Chinese seat on the Security Council in place of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (also known as Taiwan). The vote was widely seen as a sign of waning American influence in the organization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995195–197&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995195–197-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Third World nations organized themselves into the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> under the leadership of Algeria, which briefly became a dominant power at the UN.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995208–210&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995208–210-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 10 November 1975, a bloc comprising the Soviet Union and Third World nations passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_3379" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 3379">a resolution</a>, over strenuous American and Israeli opposition, declaring <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionism</a> to be a form of <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>. The resolution was repealed on 16 December 1991, shortly after the end of the Cold War.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995204–226,&#95;213,&#95;220–221&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995204–226,_213,_220–221-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With an increasing Third World presence and the failure of UN mediation in conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1965">Kashmir</a>, the UN increasingly shifted its attention to its secondary goals of economic development and cultural exchange.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995167–168,&#95;224–225&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995167–168,_224–225-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the 1970s, the UN budget for social and economic development was far greater than its peacekeeping budget.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Post-Cold_War_(1991–present)"><span id="Post-Cold_War_.281991.E2.80.93present.29"></span>Post-Cold War (1991–present)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kofi_Annan_2012_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/500px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2255" data-file-height="2828" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, secretary-general from 1997 to 2006</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_Members_Flags2.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UN_Members_Flags2.JPG/250px-UN_Members_Flags2.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UN_Members_Flags2.JPG/500px-UN_Members_Flags2.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="1232" /></a><figcaption>Flags of member nations at the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">United Nations Headquarters</a>, pictured in 2007</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UN70.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/UN70.JPG/250px-UN70.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/UN70.JPG/500px-UN70.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a><figcaption>Marking of the UN's 70th anniversary – Budapest, 2015</figcaption></figure>
<p>After the Cold War, the UN saw a radical expansion in its peacekeeping duties, taking on more missions in five years than it had in the previous four decades.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Between 1988 and 2000, the number of adopted Security Council resolutions more than doubled, and the peacekeeping budget increased more than tenfold.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200443&#95;63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200443-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334&#95;64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN negotiated an end to the <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a>, launched a successful <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transition_Assistance_Group" title="United Nations Transition Assistance Group">peacekeeping mission in Namibia</a>, and oversaw democratic elections in post-<a href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Apartheid in South Africa">apartheid</a> South Africa and post-<a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> Cambodia.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995252–256&#95;66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995252–256-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1991, the UN authorized a <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">US-led coalition</a> that repulsed Iraq's <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invasion of Kuwait</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995264–277&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995264–277-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Urquhart" title="Brian Urquhart">Brian Urquhart</a>, the under-secretary-general of the UN from 1971 to 1985, later described the hopes raised by these successes as a "false renaissance" for the organization, given the more troubled missions that followed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334&#95;64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in the last decades of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, critics of the UN condemned the organization for perceived mismanagement and corruption.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995226–227&#95;68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995226–227-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1984, American president <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> withdrew the United States' funding from the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization</a> (or UNESCO) over allegations of mismanagement, followed by the United Kingdom and Singapore.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995234–237&#95;69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995234–237-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boutros_Boutros-Ghali" title="Boutros Boutros-Ghali">Boutros Boutros-Ghali</a>, the secretary-general from 1992 to 1996, initiated a reform of the Secretariat, somewhat reducing the size of the organization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995285–286&#95;71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995285–286-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NST&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NST-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His successor, <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, initiated further management reforms in the face of threats from the US to withhold its UN dues.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NST&#95;72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NST-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Though the UN Charter had been written primarily to prevent aggression by one nation against another, in the early 1990s the UN faced several simultaneous, serious crises within Somalia, Haiti, Mozambique, and the nations that previously made up Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200766–67&#95;73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200766–67-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_Somalia_II" title="United Nations Operation in Somalia II">UN mission in Somalia</a> was widely viewed as a failure after the United States' withdrawal following casualties in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mogadishu_(1993)" title="Battle of Mogadishu (1993)">Battle of Mogadishu</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">UN mission to Bosnia</a> faced worldwide ridicule for its indecisive and confused mission in the face of ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Assistance_Mission_for_Rwanda" title="United Nations Assistance Mission for Rwanda">UN Assistance Mission for Rwanda</a> failed to intervene in the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a> amidst indecision in the Security Council.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007104&#95;75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007104-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From the late 1990s to the early 2000s, international interventions authorized by the UN took a wider variety of forms. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244</a> authorized the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> beginning in 1999. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sierra_Leone" title="United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone">UN mission</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a> was supplemented by a <a href="/wiki/British_military_intervention_in_the_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="British military intervention in the Sierra Leone Civil War">British military intervention</a>. The <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">invasion of Afghanistan in 2001</a> was overseen by NATO.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007110–111&#95;76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007110–111-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2003, the United States <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invaded Iraq</a> despite failing to pass a UN Security Council resolution for authorization, prompting a new round of questioning of the UN's effectiveness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007111&#95;77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007111-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Under the eighth secretary-general, <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, the UN intervened with peacekeepers in crises such as the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">War in Darfur</a> in Sudan and the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a> in the Democratic Republic of the Congo and sent observers and chemical weapons inspectors to the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General%27s_Internal_Review_Panel_on_United_Nations_Action_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Secretary-General&#39;s Internal Review Panel on United Nations Action in Sri Lanka">an internal review</a> of UN actions in <a href="/wiki/Alleged_war_crimes_during_the_final_stages_of_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Alleged war crimes during the final stages of the Sri Lankan Civil War">the final battles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_civil_war" title="Sri Lankan civil war">Sri Lankan Civil War</a> in 2009 concluded that the organization had suffered a "systemic failure".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2010, the organization suffered the worst loss of life in its history, when 101 personnel died in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">Haiti earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones2001to2010&#95;80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones2001to2010-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Acting under the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973</a> in 2011, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> countries intervened in the <a href="/wiki/First_Libyan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First Libyan Civil War">First Libyan Civil War</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Summit" title="Millennium Summit">Millennium Summit</a> was held in 2000 to discuss the UN's role in the 21st century.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BBCagenda&#95;81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCagenda-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The three-day meeting was the largest gathering of world leaders in history, and it culminated in the adoption by all member states of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> (or MDGs), a commitment to achieve international development in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>. Progress towards these goals, which were to be met by 2015, was ultimately uneven. The <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Summit" title="2005 World Summit">2005 World Summit</a> reaffirmed the UN's focus on promoting development, peacekeeping, human rights and global security.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> (or SDGs) were launched in 2015 to succeed the Millennium Development Goals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sustainable&#95;Development&#95;Goals&#95;83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Development_Goals-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UN_Land_Cruiser._Dnipro.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/UN_Land_Cruiser._Dnipro.jpg/250px-UN_Land_Cruiser._Dnipro.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/UN_Land_Cruiser._Dnipro.jpg/500px-UN_Land_Cruiser._Dnipro.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2731" data-file-height="1634" /></a><figcaption>UN car in Dnipro, Ukraine</figcaption></figure>
<p>In addition to addressing global challenges, the UN has sought to improve its accountability and democratic legitimacy by engaging more with <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> and fostering a global constituency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In an effort to enhance transparency, in 2016 the organization held its first public debate between candidates for secretary-general.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 1 January 2017, Portuguese diplomat <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, who had previously served as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UN High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, became the ninth secretary-general. Guterres has highlighted several key goals for his administration, including an emphasis on diplomacy for preventing conflicts, more effective peacekeeping efforts, and streamlining the organization to be more responsive and versatile to international needs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 June 2019, the UN signed a Strategic Partnership Framework with the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> in order to "jointly accelerate" the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/2030_Agenda_for_Sustainable_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development">2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout most of its history, the UN has faced funding issues. However, they have become severe since 2020, and in 2025, the UN began facing a financial crisis resulting from delays in member state due payments and refusal to pay the amount the UN charges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A major problem is that the United States, the largest contributor, has a law in place since 1994 where it will not pay more than 25% of total UN Peacekeeping fees, however it is currently assessed 27%. Additionally, the US and the second largest contributor, China, often delay their payments in order to influence the UN on topics such as the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_war" title="Gaza war">Gaza war</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Uyghurs_in_China" title="Persecution of Uyghurs in China">Persecution of Uyghurs in China</a>. Other countries have begun to follow suit, triggering a financial crisis.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 19 May 2025, only 61 countries paid their dues on time and in full.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The crisis is causing massive budget cuts within the UN, with the UN warning that millions of lives are being put at risk.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Structure">Structure</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a></div>
<p>The United Nations is part of the broader UN System, which includes an extensive network of institutions and entities. Central to the organization are five principal organs established by the UN Charter: the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">UN Secretariat</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20043–4&#95;93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20043–4-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A sixth principal organ, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a>, suspended its operations on 1 November 1994 upon the independence of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>; the last remaining UN trustee territory.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20048&#95;94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20048-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Four of the five principal organs are located at the main UN Headquarters in New York City, while the International Court of Justice is seated in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most other major agencies are based in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">UN offices at Geneva</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Vienna" title="United Nations Office at Vienna">Vienna</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Nairobi" title="United Nations Office at Nairobi">Nairobi</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and additional UN institutions are located throughout the world. The six <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of the UN, used in intergovernmental meetings and documents, are <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-langs&#95;99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-langs-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Privileges_and_Immunities_of_the_United_Nations" title="Convention on the Privileges and Immunities of the United Nations">Convention on the Privileges and Immunities of the United Nations</a>, the UN and its agencies are <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_immunity" title="Diplomatic immunity">immune</a> from the laws of the countries where they operate, safeguarding the UN's impartiality with regard to host and member countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Below the six organs are, in the words of the author Linda Fasulo, "an amazing collection of entities and organizations, some of which are actually older than the UN itself and operate with almost complete independence from it".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044&#95;101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These include specialized agencies, research and training institutions, programmes and funds and other UN entities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044–7&#95;102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044–7-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>All organizations in the UN system obey the <i>Noblemaire principle</i>, which calls for salaries that will attract and retain citizens of countries where compensation is highest, and which ensures equal pay for work of equal value regardless of the employee's nationality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-un-salaries&#95;103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-salaries-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In practice, the <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Service_Commission" title="International Civil Service Commission">International Civil Service Commission</a>, which governs the conditions of UN personnel, takes reference to the highest-paying national civil service.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Staff salaries are subject to an internal tax that is administered by the UN organizations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-un-salaries&#95;103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-salaries-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>

<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:NYC24-158_UN.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="UN General Assembly hall"><img alt="UN General Assembly hall" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/NYC24-158_UN.jpg/330px-NYC24-158_UN.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/NYC24-158_UN.jpg/500px-NYC24-158_UN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/NYC24-158_UN.jpg/960px-NYC24-158_UN.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3080" /></a></span></div></div></div>

<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-0px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City,_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Headquarters of the UN in New York City"><img alt="Headquarters of the UN in New York City" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/330px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/500px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/960px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3144" data-file-height="1611" /></a></span></div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-25px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="International Court of Justice"><img alt="International Court of Justice" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg/330px-International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="194" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg/500px-International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg/960px-International_Court_of_Justice_HQ_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1194" /></a></span></div></div></div>
</td></tr>
<tr style="vertical-align:top; font-size:95%;">
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>May resolve non-compulsory recommendations to states or suggestions to the Security Council (UNSC);</li>
<li>Decides on the admission of new members, following proposal by the UNSC;</li>
<li>Adopts the budget;</li>
<li>Elects the non-permanent members of the UNSC; all members of the Economic and Social Council; the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a> (following their proposal by the UNSC); and the fifteen judges of the International Court of Justice (ICJ). Each country has one vote.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>Supports the other <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">UN bodies</a> administratively (for example, in the organization of conferences, the writing of reports and studies and the preparation of the budget);</li>
<li>Its chairperson—the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a>—is elected by the General Assembly for a five-year mandate and is the UN's foremost representative.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>Decides disputes between states that recognize its jurisdiction;</li>
<li>Issues legal opinions;</li>
<li>Renders judgment by <a href="/wiki/Relative_majority" class="mw-redirect" title="Relative majority">relative majority</a>. Its fifteen judges are elected by the UN General Assembly for nine-year terms.</li></ul>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="7" style="background:white;">
</td></tr>
