<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-top:10px;"><b><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a></b><br />&#8212;&#160;For international security issues&#160;&#8212;
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-top:10px;"><b><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">UN Economic and Social Council</a></b><br />&#8212;&#160;For global economic and social affairs&#160;&#8212;
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-top:10px;"><b><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">UN Trusteeship Council</a></b><br />&#8212;&#160;For administering <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_trust_territories" title="United Nations trust territories">trust territories</a> (<i>currently inactive</i>)&#160;&#8212;
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-50px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="UN security council"><img alt="UN security council" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg/330px-UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="195" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg/500px-UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg/960px-UN-Sicherheitsrat_-_UN_Security_Council_-_New_York_City_-_2014_01_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a></span></div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-20px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="UN Economic and Social Council"><img alt="UN Economic and Social Council" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/330px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="260" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/500px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/960px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3253" data-file-height="1746" /></a></span></div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:0px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="UN Trusteeship Council"><img alt="UN Trusteeship Council" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/330px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="260" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/500px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/960px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="1696" /></a></span></div></div></div>
</td></tr>
<tr style="vertical-align:top;font-size:95%;">
<td style="padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>Responsible for the maintenance of <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">international peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_security" title="International security">security</a>;</li>
<li>May adopt <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">compulsory resolutions</a>;</li>
<li>Has fifteen members: <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">five permanent members</a> with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto power</a> and ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="List of members of the United Nations Security Council">elected members</a>.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>Responsible for co-operation between states as regards economic and social matters;</li>
<li>Co-ordinates co-operation between the UN's numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies</a>;</li>
<li>Has 54 members, elected by the General Assembly to serve staggered three-year mandates.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;">
<ul><li>Was originally designed to manage colonial possessions that were former <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>;</li>
<li>Has been inactive since 1994, when <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, the last trust territory, attained independence.</li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="General_Assembly">General Assembly</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/250px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="170" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/500px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5221" data-file-height="3544" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, leader of the Soviet Union, addressing the UN General Assembly in December 1988</figcaption></figure>
<p>The General Assembly is the primary <a href="/wiki/Deliberative_assembly" title="Deliberative assembly">deliberative assembly</a> of the UN. Composed of all <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a>, the assembly gathers at annual sessions at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations General Assembly Hall">General Assembly Hall</a>, but emergency sessions can be summoned.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The assembly is led by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="President of the United Nations General Assembly">president</a>, elected by the member states on a rotating regional basis, and 21 vice-presidents.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200469–70&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200469–70-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first session convened on 10 January 1946 in the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Central_Hall,_Westminster" title="Methodist Central Hall, Westminster">Methodist Central Hall</a> in London and comprised representatives of 51 nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unmilestones1941to1950&#95;35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When the General Assembly decides on seminal questions such as those on peace and security, admission of new members and budgetary matters, a two-thirds majority of those present and voting is required.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All other questions are decided by a majority vote. Each member has one vote. Apart from the approval of budgetary matters, resolutions are not binding on the members. The Assembly may make recommendations on any matters within the scope of the UN, except matters of peace and security that are under consideration by the Security Council.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133&#95;108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Draft resolutions can be forwarded to the General Assembly by its six main committees:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200470–73&#95;112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200470–73-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_First_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="General Assembly First Committee">First Committee (Disarmament and International Security)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Second_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Second Committee">Second Committee (Economic and Financial)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Third_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Third Committee">Third Committee (Social, Humanitarian, and Cultural)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fourth_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Fourth Committee">Fourth Committee (Special Political and Decolonization)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Fifth_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Fifth Committee">Fifth Committee (Administrative and Budgetary)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Sixth_Committee_(Legal)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations General Assembly Sixth Committee (Legal)">Sixth Committee (Legal)</a></li></ul>
<p>As well as by the following two committees:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Committee" title="United Nations General Committee">General Committee</a> – a supervisory committee consisting of the assembly's president, vice-presidents, and committee heads</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Credentials_Committee" title="United Nations Credentials Committee">Credentials Committee</a> – responsible for determining the credentials of each member nation's UN representatives</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Security_Council">Security Council</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg/250px-Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="170" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="171" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a>, demonstrates a vial with <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_of_the_2003_invasion_of_Iraq#Weapons_of_Mass_Destruction" class="mw-redirect" title="Legitimacy of the 2003 invasion of Iraq">alleged</a> Iraq <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon">chemical weapon</a> probes to the UN Security Council on <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_and_the_Iraq_War" title="United Nations Security Council and the Iraq War">Iraq war</a> hearings, 5 February 2003.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Security Council is charged with maintaining peace and security among nations. While other organs of the UN can only make recommendations to member states, the Security Council has the power to make binding decisions that member states have agreed to carry out, under the terms of Charter Article 25.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Chapter&#124;V&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter|V-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The decisions of the council are known as <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">United Nations Security Council resolutions</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200439–43&#95;114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200439–43-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Security Council is made up of fifteen member states: five permanent members (China, France, Russia, the United Kingdom and the United States) and ten non-permanent members (<a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Korea">Republic of Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, as of 2025<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_Nations&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>). The five permanent members hold <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto power</a> over UN resolutions, allowing a permanent member to block adoption of a resolution, though not debate. The ten temporary seats are held for two-year terms, with five members elected each year by the General Assembly on a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Regional_Groups" title="United Nations Regional Groups">regional basis</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200440–41&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200440–41-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The presidency of the Security Council rotates alphabetically each month.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="UN_Secretariat">UN Secretariat</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres,_23.03.23.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg/250px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="285" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg/330px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg/500px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres%2C_23.03.23.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2667" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, the current <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The UN Secretariat carries out the day-to-day duties required to operate and maintain the UN system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is composed of tens of thousands of international civil servants worldwide and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a>, who is assisted by the <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Deputy Secretary-General of the United Nations">deputy secretary-general</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200421&#95;118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200421-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Secretariat's duties include providing information and facilities needed by UN bodies for their meetings and carrying out tasks as directed by the Security Council, the General Assembly, the Economic and Social Council, and other UN bodies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009285&#95;119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009285-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The secretary-general acts as the spokesperson and leader of the UN. The position is defined in the UN Charter as the organization's chief administrative officer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Article 99 of the charter states that the secretary-general can bring to the Security Council's attention "any matter which in their opinion may threaten the maintenance of international peace and security", a phrase that secretaries-general since <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a> have interpreted as giving the position broad scope for action on the world stage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199531–32&#95;121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199531–32-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The office has evolved into a dual role of an administrator of the UN organization and a diplomat and mediator addressing disputes between member states and finding consensus to <a href="/wiki/List_of_global_issues" title="List of global issues">global issues</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200759–62&#95;122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200759–62-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The secretary-general is appointed by the General Assembly, after being recommended by the Security Council, where the permanent members have veto power. There are no specific criteria for the post, but over the years it has become accepted that the position shall be held for one or two terms of five years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The current secretary-general is <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> of Portugal, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> in 2017.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="International_Court_of_Justice">International Court of Justice</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg/250px-Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg/500px-Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>The ICJ ruled that <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Kosovo's unilateral declaration of independence</a> from Serbia in 2008 did not violate international law.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The International Court of Justice (or ICJ), sometimes known as the World Court,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-britannica.com&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is the primary judicial organ of the UN. It is the successor to the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_International_Justice" title="Permanent Court of International Justice">Permanent Court of International Justice</a> and occupies the body's former headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">Peace Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague, Netherlands</a>, making it the only principal organ not based in New York City. The ICJ's main function is adjudicating disputes among nations. Examples of issues they have heard include war crimes, violations of state sovereignty and ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The court can also be called upon by other UN organs to provide advisory opinions on matters of international law.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183&#95;127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All UN member states are parties to the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_the_International_Court_of_Justice" title="Statute of the International Court of Justice">ICJ Statute</a>, which forms an integral part of the UN Charter, and non-members may also become parties. The ICJ's rulings are binding upon parties and, along with its advisory opinions, serve as <a href="/wiki/Sources_of_international_law" title="Sources of international law">sources of international law</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-britannica.com&#95;125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The court is composed of 15 judges appointed to nine-year terms by the General Assembly. Every sitting judge must be from a different nation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183&#95;127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004100–101&#95;128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004100–101-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Economic_and_Social_Council">Economic and Social Council</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">United Nations Economic and Social Council</a></div>
<p>The Economic and Social Council (or the ECOSOC) assists the General Assembly in promoting international economic and social co-operation and development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was established to serve as the UN's primary forum for global issues and is the largest and most complex UN body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The ECOSOC's functions include gathering data, conducting studies and advising and making recommendations to member states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104&#95;130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its work is carried out primarily by subsidiary bodies focused on a wide variety of topics. These include the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Permanent_Forum_on_Indigenous_Issues" title="United Nations Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues">United Nations Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues</a>, which advises UN agencies on issues relating to <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Forum_on_Forests" title="United Nations Forum on Forests">United Nations Forum on Forests</a>, which coordinates and promotes sustainable forest management, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistical_Commission" title="United Nations Statistical Commission">United Nations Statistical Commission</a>, which co-ordinates information-gathering efforts between agencies, and the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Sustainable_Development" title="Commission on Sustainable Development">Commission on Sustainable Development</a>, which co-ordinates efforts between UN agencies and NGOs working towards <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>. ECOSOC may also grant consultative status to non-governmental organizations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104&#95;130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of April 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_Nations&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> almost 5,600 organizations have this status.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004156&#95;132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004156-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Specialized_agencies">Specialized agencies</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">List of specialized agencies of the United Nations</a></div>
<p>The UN Charter stipulates that each primary organ of the United Nations can establish various specialized agencies to fulfill its duties.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CharterIX&#95;134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CharterIX-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Specialized agencies are autonomous organizations working with the United Nations and each other through the coordinating machinery of the Economic and Social Council. Each was integrated into the UN system through an agreement with the UN under UN Charter article 57.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CEB&#95;135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEB-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are fifteen specialized agencies, which perform functions as diverse as facilitating international travel, preventing and addressing pandemics, and promoting economic development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>c<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<td>3</td>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Funds,_programmes,_and_other_bodies"><span id="Funds.2C_programmes.2C_and_other_bodies"></span>Funds, programmes, and other bodies</h3></div>
<p>The United Nations system includes a myriad of autonomous, separately administered <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System#Funds_and_programmes,_research_and_training_institutes,_and_other_bodies" title="United Nations System">funds, programmes, research and training institutes, and other subsidiary bodies</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-un.org&#95;138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each of these entities have their own area of work, governance structure, and budgets such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (or the WTO) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (or the IAEA), operate independently of the UN but maintain formal partnership agreements. The UN performs much of its humanitarian work through these institutions, such as preventing famine and malnutrition (the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>), protecting vulnerable and displaced people (the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UNHCR</a>), and combating the HIV/AIDS pandemic (the <a href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS">UNAIDS</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004171–177&#95;139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004171–177-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; text-align:left;">
<caption style="padding-top:1em;">Programmes and funds of the United Nations
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Acronyms
</th>

</th>

</th>

</th>
<th>Established
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>
</td>
<td><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/60px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, United States
