<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Membership">Membership</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">Member states of the United Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_from_the_United_Nations" title="Expulsion from the United Nations">Expulsion from the United Nations</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_(Member_States_and_Territories).svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg/500px-United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="380" height="193" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg/960px-United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="2756" data-file-height="1399" /></a><figcaption> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#009edb; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#9edb00; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;2 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">UN Observer States</a> (Palestine, Holy See)</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#db9e00; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;2 eligible Non-Member States (Niue, Cook Islands)</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#c0c0c0; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;17 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_non-self-governing_territories" title="United Nations list of non-self-governing territories">non-self-governing territories</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#f0f0f0; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a></div> </figcaption></figure>
<p>All the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">undisputed</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">independent states</a> are members of the United Nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-UN&#95;SouthSudan&#95;193rd&#95;state&#95;140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_SouthSudan_193rd_state-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, which joined 14 July 2011, is the most recent addition, bringing a total of 193 UN member states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-members&#95;2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-members-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN Charter outlines the membership rules:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote">
<ol><li>Membership in the United Nations is open to all other peace-loving states that accept the obligations contained in the present Charter and, in the judgment of the Organization, are able and willing to carry out these obligations.</li>
<li>The admission of any such state to membership in the United Nations will be effected by a decision of the General Assembly upon the recommendation of the Security Council. Chapter II, Article 4.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ol></blockquote>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Presiden_Sukarno_(retouched).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg/250px-Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="289" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg/330px-Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg/500px-Presiden_Sukarno_%28retouched%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3156" data-file-height="4557" /></a><figcaption>Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, Indonesia was <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_and_the_United_Nations#Withdrawal_in_1965" title="Indonesia and the United Nations">the first and only country that attempted</a> to leave the United Nations.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In addition, there are two <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">non-member observer states</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">Palestine</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Non-member&#95;States&#95;3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Non-member_States-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>d<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">states in free association</a> with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, are full members of several UN specialized agencies and have had their "full treaty-making capacity" recognized by the Secretariat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-art102&#95;143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art102-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> was the first and the only nation that attempted to withdraw its membership from the United Nations, in protest to the election of Malaysia as a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> in 1965 during <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation">conflict between the two countries</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After forming <a href="/wiki/CONEFO" title="CONEFO">CONEFO</a> as a short-lived rival to the UN, Indonesia resumed its membership in 1966.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Group_of_77">Group of 77</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a></div>
<p>The Group of 77 (or the G77) at the UN is a loose coalition of <a href="/wiki/Developing_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing nations">developing nations</a> that is designed to promote its members' collective economic interests and create an enhanced joint negotiating capacity in the UN. Seventy-seven nations founded the organization, but by November 2013 the organization had since expanded to 133 member countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The group was founded 15 June 1964 by the "Joint Declaration of the Seventy-Seven Countries" issued at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">United Nations Conference on Trade and Development</a> (or the UNCTAD). The group held its first major meeting in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> in 1967, where it adopted the Charter of Algiers and established the basis for permanent institutional structures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">New International Economic Order</a> by developing countries in the 1970s, the work of the G77 spread throughout the UN system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similar groupings of developing states also operate in other UN agencies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">Group of 24</a> (or the G-24), which operates in the IMF on monetary affairs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Objectives">Objectives</h2></div>
<p>The overarching strategy of the United Nations is captured in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Common_Agenda" title="United Nations Common Agenda">United Nations Common Agenda</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Peacekeeping_and_security">Peacekeeping and security</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations peacekeeping</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Nations_peacekeeping_missions" title="List of United Nations peacekeeping missions">List of United Nations peacekeeping missions</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg/250px-United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="190" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg/330px-United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg/500px-United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Helmet_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="159" /></a><figcaption>United Nations Peacekeeping Logo</figcaption></figure>
<p>The UN, after approval by the Security Council, sends peacekeepers to regions where armed conflict has recently ceased or paused to enforce the terms of peace agreements and to discourage combatants from resuming hostilities. Since the UN does not maintain its own military, peacekeeping forces are voluntarily provided by member states. These soldiers are sometimes nicknamed "Blue Helmets" because they wear distinctive blue helmets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200452&#95;151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200452-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTECoulon1998ix&#95;152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoulon1998ix-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Peacekeeping forces as a whole received the Nobel Peace Prize in 1988.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The UN has carried out 71 peacekeeping operations since 1947, and As of April 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_Nations&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, over 88,000 peacekeeping personnel from 121 nations have been deployed on missions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest is the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_South_Sudan" title="United Nations Mission in South Sudan">United Nations Mission in South Sudan</a> (or UNMISS), which has close to 19,200 uniformed personnel,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the smallest, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Military_Observer_Group_in_India_and_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Military Observer Group in India and Pakistan">United Nations Military Observer Group in India and Pakistan</a> (or UNMOGIP), consists of 113 civilians and experts charged with monitoring the ceasefire in <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(state)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (state)">Jammu and Kashmir</a>. UN peacekeepers with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Truce_Supervision_Organization" title="United Nations Truce Supervision Organization">United Nations Truce Supervision Organization</a> (or UNTSO) have been stationed in the Middle East since 1948, the longest-running active peacekeeping mission.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-UNPO&#95;156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A study by the RAND Corporation in 2005 found the UN to be successful in two-thirds of its peacekeeping efforts. It compared efforts at nation-building by the UN to those of the United States and found that 87.5% of UN cases are at peace, as compared with 50% of U.S. cases at peace.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also in 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Security_Report_2005" title="Human Security Report 2005">Human Security Report</a> documented a decline in the number of wars, <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocides</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_abuses" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights abuses">human rights abuses</a> since the end of the Cold War, and presented evidence, albeit circumstantial, that international activism – mostly spearheaded by the UN – has been the main cause of the decline in armed conflict.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Situations in which the UN has not only acted to keep the peace but also intervened include the Korean War and the authorization of intervention in Iraq after the Gulf War.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200756&#95;159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200756-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Further studies published between 2008 and 2021 determined UN peacekeeping operations to be more effective at ensuring long-lasting peace and minimizing civilian casualties.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="inaction&#95;on&#95;genocide&#95;and&#95;human&#95;rights"></span>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG/250px-GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG" decoding="async" width="240" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG/500px-GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/UN_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Buffer Zone in Cyprus">UN Buffer Zone in Cyprus</a> was established in 1974 following the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkish invasion of Cyprus</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The UN has also drawn criticism for perceived failures. In many cases, member states have shown reluctance to achieve or enforce Security Council resolutions. Disagreements in the Security Council about military action and intervention are seen as having failed to prevent the <a href="/wiki/1971_Bangladesh_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="1971 Bangladesh Genocide">Bangladesh genocide in 1971</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBall201146&#95;161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBall201146-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_rule_of_Cambodia" class="mw-redirect" title="Khmer Rouge rule of Cambodia">Cambodian genocide</a> in the 1970s,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007187&#95;162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007187-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Rwandan genocide in 1994.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007102–105&#95;163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007102–105-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly, UN inaction is blamed for failing to either prevent the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a> or complete the peacekeeping operations during the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995294–311&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995294–311-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> UN peacekeepers have also been accused of child rape, soliciting prostitutes, and sexual abuse during various peacekeeping missions in the Democratic Republic of the Congo,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Haiti,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Liberia,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Sudan,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Burundi, and Côte d'Ivoire.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Scientists cited UN peacekeepers from Nepal as the source of the <a href="/wiki/2010s_Haiti_cholera_outbreak" title="2010s Haiti cholera outbreak">2010s Haiti cholera outbreak</a>, which killed more than 8,000 people.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff,_Haiti,_Feb._20,_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg/250px-A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="179" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg/500px-A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2587" data-file-height="1848" /></a><figcaption>A Nepalese soldier on a peacekeeping deployment providing security at a rice distribution site in Haiti during 2010</figcaption></figure>
<p>In addition to peacekeeping, the UN is also active in encouraging <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a>. Regulation of armaments was included in the writing of the UN Charter in 1945 and was envisioned as a way of limiting the use of human and economic resources for their creation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Chapter&#124;V&#95;113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter|V-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The advent of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> came only weeks after the signing of the charter, resulting in the first <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution">resolution</a> of the first <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="General Assembly">General Assembly</a> meeting calling for specific proposals for "the elimination from national armaments of atomic weapons and of all other major weapons adaptable to mass destruction".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN has been involved with arms-limitation treaties such as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty" title="Outer Space Treaty">Outer Space Treaty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seabed_Arms_Control_Treaty" title="Seabed Arms Control Treaty">Seabed Arms Control Treaty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Biological_Weapons_Convention" title="Biological Weapons Convention">Biological Weapons Convention</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">Chemical Weapons Convention</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Treaty" title="Ottawa Treaty">Ottawa Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004188–189&#95;172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004188–189-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Three UN bodies oversee arms proliferation issues: the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty_Organization_Preparatory_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization Preparatory Commission">Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization Preparatory Commission</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004189–190&#95;173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004189–190-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, many peacekeeping missions focus on disarmament: several operations in West Africa disarmed roughly 250,000 former combatants and secured tens of thousands of weapons and millions of munitions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Human_rights">Human rights</h3></div>
<p>One of the UN's primary purposes is "promoting and encouraging respect for human rights and for fundamental freedoms for all without distinction as to race, sex, language, or religion", and member states pledge to undertake "joint and separate action" to protect these rights.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CharterIX&#95;134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CharterIX-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Charter1&#95;175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter1-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR.jpg/250px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="196" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR.jpg/500px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5912" data-file-height="4640" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, 1949</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1948, the General Assembly adopted a <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, drafted by a committee headed by American diplomat and activist <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>, and including the French lawyer <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Cassin" title="René Cassin">René Cassin</a>. The document proclaims basic civil, political and economic rights common to all human beings, though its effectiveness towards achieving these ends has been disputed since its drafting.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007178–182&#95;176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007178–182-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Declaration serves as a "common standard of achievement for all people and all nations" rather than a legally binding document, but it has become the basis of two binding treaties, the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights" title="International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights" title="International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights">International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009377&#95;177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009377-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In practice, the UN is unable to take significant action against human rights abuses without a Security Council resolution, though it does substantial work in investigating and reporting abuses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007185,&#95;188&#95;178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007185,_188-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1979, the General Assembly adopted the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_against_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women</a>; followed by the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a> in 1989.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand200970,&#95;73&#95;179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand200970,_73-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the end of the Cold War, the push for human rights action took on new impetus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007192&#95;180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007192-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">United Nations Commission on Human Rights</a> was formed in 1993 to oversee human rights issues for the UN, following the recommendation of that year's <a href="/wiki/World_Conference_on_Human_Rights" title="World Conference on Human Rights">World Conference on Human Rights</a>. Jacques Fomerand, a scholar of the UN, describes the organization's mandate as "broad and vague", with only "meagre" resources to carry it out.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009347&#95;181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009347-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2006, it was replaced by a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">Human Rights Council</a> consisting of 47 nations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also in 2006, the General Assembly passed a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Rights_of_Indigenous_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Rights of Indigenous Peoples">Declaration on the Rights of Indigenous People</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in 2011 it passed its first resolution recognizing the rights of members of the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT">LGBTQ+</a> community.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Other UN bodies responsible for <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women&#39;s rights">women's rights</a> issues include the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_the_Status_of_Women" title="United Nations Commission on the Status of Women">United Nations Commission on the Status of Women</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Fund_for_Women" title="United Nations Development Fund for Women">United Nations Development Fund for Women</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_International_Research_and_Training_Institute_for_the_Advancement_of_Women" title="United Nations International Research and Training Institute for the Advancement of Women">United Nations International Research and Training Institute for the Advancement of Women</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand200957,&#95;194,&#95;341&#95;185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand200957,_194,_341-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues, one of three bodies with a mandate to oversee issues related to indigenous peoples, held its first session in 2002.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Economic_development_and_humanitarian_assistance">Economic development and humanitarian assistance</h3></div>
<table style="background:#f3f9ff; padding-left:7px; padding-bottom:7px; float:right; border:1px dashed #aaa; margin-left:1em; margin-bottom:1em;">

<tbody><tr>
<td colspan="2">
<p>Millennium Development Goals<sup id="cite&#95;ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top; font-size:90%;">
<ol><li>Eradicate extreme poverty and hunger</li>
<li>Achieve universal primary education</li>
<li>Promote gender equality and empower women</li>
<li>Reduce child mortality</li>
<li>Improve maternal health</li>
<li>Combat HIV/AIDS, malaria, and other diseases</li>
<li>Ensure environmental sustainability</li>
<li>Develop a global partnership for development</li></ol>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Another primary purpose of the UN is "to achieve international co-operation in solving international problems of an economic, social, cultural and humanitarian character".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Charter1&#95;175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter1-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Numerous bodies have been created to work towards this goal, primarily under the authority of the General Assembly and the ECOSOC.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007143–144&#95;188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007143–144-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2000, the 192 UN member states agreed to achieve eight <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> by 2015.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> were launched in 2015 to succeed the Millennium Development Goals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sustainable&#95;Development&#95;Goals&#95;83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Development_Goals-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The SDGs have an associated financing framework called the <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa_Action_Agenda" title="Addis Ababa Action Agenda">Addis Ababa Action Agenda</a>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/250px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/500px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2220" /></a><figcaption>Three former directors of the <a href="/wiki/Smallpox#Eradication" title="Smallpox">Global Smallpox Eradication Programme</a> reading the news that smallpox has been globally eradicated in 1980</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UN Development Programme</a> (or the UNDP), an organization for grant-based technical assistance, is one of the leading bodies in the field of <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">international development</a>. The organization also publishes the UN <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, a comparative measure <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">ranking countries</a> by poverty, literacy, education, life expectancy, and other factors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004169–170,&#95;172&#95;190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004169–170,_172-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009341–342&#95;191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009341–342-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (or the FAO) promotes agricultural development and food security.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009126&#95;192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009126-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">United Nations Children's Fund</a> (or UNICEF) was created in 1946 to aid European children after the Second World War and expanded its mission to provide aid around the world and to uphold the convention on the Rights of the Child.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (or the IMF) are independent, specialized agencies and observers within the UN framework.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They were initially formed separately from the UN through the <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">Bretton Woods Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The World Bank provides loans for international development, while the IMF promotes international economic co-operation and gives emergency loans to indebted countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009175,&#95;191–192&#95;197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009175,_191–192-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg/250px-Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg/500px-Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a><figcaption>In <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, UNHCR remains responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian refugees">Syrian refugees</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zaatari_refugee_camp" title="Zaatari refugee camp">Zaatari refugee camp</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (or WHO), which focuses on international health issues and disease eradication, is another of the UN's largest agencies. In 1980, the agency announced that the eradication of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> had been completed. In subsequent decades, <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a> eradicated <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_blindness" class="mw-redirect" title="River blindness">river blindness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leprosy" title="Leprosy">leprosy</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004176–177&#95;198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004176–177-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS">Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS</a> (or UNAIDS) coordinated the organization's response to the AIDS epidemic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009199–200&#95;199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009199–200-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/UN_Population_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Population Fund">UN Population Fund</a>, which also dedicates part of its resources to combating HIV, is the world's largest source of funding for <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Reproductive health">reproductive health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009368&#95;200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009368-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Along with the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a>, the UN takes a leading role in coordinating emergency relief.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183&#95;201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (or the WFP) provides food aid in response to famine, natural disasters, and armed conflict. The organization feeds an average of 90 million people in 80 nations per year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183&#95;201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (or the UNHCR) works to protect the rights of refugees, asylum seekers and stateless people.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UNHCR and the WFP programmes are funded by voluntary contributions from governments, corporations, and individuals, though the UNHCR's administrative costs are paid for by the UN's primary budget.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009348,&#95;398&#95;204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009348,_398-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Environment_and_climate">Environment and climate</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a></div>
<p>Beginning with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Environmental_Programme" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Environmental Programme">UN Environmental Programme</a> (or the UNEP) in 1972, the UN has made environmental issues a prominent part of its agenda. A lack of success in the first two decades of UN work in this area led to the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">Earth Summit</a> in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil, in 1992; which sought to give new impetus to these efforts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007160–162&#95;205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007160–162-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1988, the UNEP and the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (or the WMO), another UN organization, established the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>, which assesses and reports on research on <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UN-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> set legally binding emissions reduction targets for ratifying states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004179&#95;207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004179-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other_global_issues">Other global issues</h3></div>
<p>Since the UN's creation, over 80 colonies have attained independence. The General Assembly adopted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Granting_of_Independence_to_Colonial_Countries_and_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples">Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples</a> in 1960 with no votes against but abstentions from all major colonial powers. The UN works towards decolonization through groups including the <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">UN Committee on Decolonization</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The committee lists seventeen remaining "<a href="/wiki/Non-self-governing_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-self-governing territories">non-self-governing territories</a>", the largest and most populous of which is the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The UN also declares and co-ordinates <a href="/wiki/International_observance" class="mw-redirect" title="International observance">international observances</a> that bring awareness to issues of international interest or concern; examples include <a href="/wiki/World_Tuberculosis_Day" title="World Tuberculosis Day">World Tuberculosis Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earth_Day" title="Earth Day">Earth Day</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Year_of_Deserts_and_Desertification" title="International Year of Deserts and Desertification">International Year of Deserts and Desertification</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Starting in 2023, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.un.org/digital-emerging-technologies/">United Nations Office for Digital and Emerging Technologies</a> has organized an annual UN Open Source Week to facilitate collaborative and international technological projects, AI policies, and governance.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Funding">Funding</h2></div>
