</tbody></table>
<p>The UN budget for 2024 was $3.59 billion, not including additional resources donated by members, such as peacekeeping forces.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Including <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies of the UN</a>, the UN System Chief Executives Board for Coordination reports total expenses of $67.4 billion in 2022 for 43 United Nations entities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The UN is financed from assessed and voluntary contributions from its member states. The General Assembly approves the regular budget and determines the assessment for each member. This is broadly based on the relative capacity of each nation to pay, as measured by its <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> (or GNI), with adjustments for external debt and low per capita income.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-fifth-2006&#95;216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifth-2006-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Assembly has established the principle that the UN should not be unduly dependent on any one member to finance its operations. Thus, there is a "ceiling" rate, setting the maximum amount that any member can be assessed for the regular budget. In December 2000, the Assembly revised the scale of assessments in response to pressure from the United States. As part of that revision, the regular budget ceiling was reduced from 25% to 22%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004117&#95;217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004117-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed country">least developed countries</a> (or LDCs), a ceiling rate of 0.01% is applied.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-fifth-2006&#95;216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifth-2006-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition to the ceiling rates, the minimum amount assessed to any member nation (or "floor" rate) is set at 0.001% of the UN budget ($31,000 for the two-year budget 2021–2022).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEWeissDaws2009682&#95;219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeissDaws2009682-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A large share of the UN's expenditure addresses its core mission of peace and security, and this budget is assessed separately from the main organizational budget.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004115&#95;220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004115-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The peacekeeping budget for the 2021–2022 fiscal year is $6.38 billion, supporting 66,839 personnel deployed in 12 missions worldwide.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> UN peace operations are funded by assessments, using a formula derived from the regular funding scale that includes a weighted surcharge for the five permanent Security Council members, who must approve all peacekeeping operations. This surcharge serves to offset discounted peacekeeping assessment rates for less developed countries. The largest contributors to the <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a> budget for 2023–2024 are: the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (26.94%), <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (18.68%), <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (8.03%), <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (6.11%), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (5.35%), <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (5.28%), <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (3.18%), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (2.62%), <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (2.57%) and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (2.28%).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Special UN programmes not included in the regular budget, such as <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> and the World Food Programme, are financed by voluntary contributions from member governments, corporations, and private individuals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Assessments_and_reviews">Assessments and reviews</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">Reform of the United Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Reform of the United Nations Security Council">Reform of the United Nations Security Council</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg/250px-Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg/500px-Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3078" data-file-height="2319" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/2001_Nobel_Peace_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Nobel Peace Prize">2001 Nobel Peace Prize</a> to the UN—diploma in the lobby of the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">UN Headquarters</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Several studies have examined the Security Council's responsiveness to armed conflict. Findings suggests that the council is more likely to meet and deliberate on conflicts that are more intense and have led to more humanitarian suffering, but that its responsiveness is also shaped by the political interests of member states and in particular of the permanent members.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>UN peacekeeping missions are assessed to be generally successful. A book looking at 47 peace operations by <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Page_Fortna" title="Virginia Page Fortna">Virginia Page Fortna</a> of <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> found that UN-led conflict resolution usually resulted in long-term peace.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Political scientists Hanne Fjelde, Lisa Hultman and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Desiree_Nilsson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Desiree Nilsson (page does not exist)">Desiree Nilsson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Uppsala_University" title="Uppsala University">Uppsala University</a> studied twenty years of data on peacekeeping missions, concluding that they were more effective at reducing civilian casualties than counterterrorism operations by nation states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> professor Lise Howard postulates that UN peacekeeping operations are more effective due to their emphasis on "verbal persuasion, financial inducements and coercion short of offensive military force, including surveillance and arrest", which are likelier to change the behavior of warring parties.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>British historian <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kennedy" title="Paul Kennedy">Paul Kennedy</a> states that while the organization has suffered some major setbacks, "when all its aspects are considered, the UN has brought great benefits to our generation and will bring benefits to our children's and grandchildren's generations as well."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007290&#95;228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007290-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, then French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> stated that "France trusts the United Nations. She knows that no state, no matter how powerful, can solve urgent problems, fight for development and bring an end to all crises. France wants the UN to be the centre of global governance".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In his 1953 address to the United States Committee for United Nations Day, American President Dwight D. Eisenhower expressed his view that, for all its flaws, "the United Nations represents man's best organized hope to substitute the conference table for the battlefield".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacques_Fomerand&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jacques Fomerand (page does not exist)">Jacques Fomerand</a>, a professor in political sciences, writes that the "accomplishments of the United Nations in the last 60 years are impressive in their own terms. Progress in human development during the 20th century has been dramatic, and the UN and its agencies have certainly helped the world become a more hospitable and livable place for millions".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009cviii&#95;231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009cviii-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Reviewing the first 50 years of the UN's history, the author <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanley_Meisler&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stanley Meisler (page does not exist)">Stanley Meisler</a> writes that "the United Nations never fulfilled the hopes of its founders, but it accomplished a great deal nevertheless", citing its role in decolonization and its many successful peacekeeping efforts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995339&#95;232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995339-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards">Awards</h2></div>
<p>A number of agencies and individuals associated with the UN have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> in recognition of their work. Two secretaries-general, Dag Hammarskjöld and Kofi Annan, were each awarded the prize; as were Ralph Bunche, a UN negotiator, René Cassin, a contributor to the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, and the American Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Cordell_Hull" title="Cordell Hull">Cordell Hull</a> for his role in the organization's founding. <a href="/wiki/Lester_B._Pearson" title="Lester B. Pearson">Lester B. Pearson</a>, the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_External_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for External Affairs">Secretary of State for External Affairs</a>, was awarded the prize in 1957 for his role in organizing the UN's first peacekeeping force to resolve the Suez Crisis.
</p><p>UNICEF won the prize in 1965, the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> in 1969, the UN Peacekeeping Forces in 1988, the International Atomic Energy Agency (which reports to the UN) in 2005, and the UN-supported <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a> in 2013. The UN High Commissioner for Refugees was awarded the prize in 1954 and 1981, becoming one of only two recipients to win the prize twice. The UN as a whole was awarded the prize in 2001, sharing it with Annan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a> received the prize "for their efforts to build up and disseminate greater knowledge about man-made climate change, and to lay the foundations for the measures that are needed to counteract such change."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On March 21, 2025, the joint Universities of <a href="/wiki/KU_Leuven" title="KU Leuven">Leuven</a> and <a href="/wiki/UCLouvain" title="UCLouvain">Louvain</a> (Belgium) awarded the UN an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degree" title="Honorary degree">honorary degree</a> which was given in the hands of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Criticism">Criticism</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_United_Nations" title="Criticism of the United Nations">Criticism of the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Role">Role</h3></div>
<p>In a sometimes-misquoted statement, American President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> stated in February 2003—referring to UN uncertainty towards Iraqi provocations under the Saddam Hussein regime—that "free nations will not allow the UN to fade into history as an ineffective, irrelevant debating society."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, former American President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, in his memoir <i><a href="/wiki/A_Promised_Land" title="A Promised Land">A Promised Land</a></i> noted, "In the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the chances of reaching any consensus had been slim, which is why the UN had stood idle as <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Soviet tanks rolled into Hungary</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">U.S. planes dropped napalm on the Vietnamese countryside</a>. Even after the Cold War, divisions within the Security Council continued to hamstring the UN's ability to tackle problems. Its member states lacked either the means or the collective will to reconstruct failing states like <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, or prevent an ethnic slaughter in places like Sri Lanka."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since its founding, there have been many calls for <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">reform of the UN</a> but little consensus on how to do so. Some want the UN to play a greater or more effective role in world affairs, while others want its role reduced to humanitarian work.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Representation_and_structure">Representation and structure</h3></div>
<p>Core features of the UN apparatus, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto</a> privileges of some nations in the <a href="/wiki/Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Council">Security Council</a>, are often described as fundamentally undemocratic, contrary to the UN mission, and a main cause of inaction on genocides and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jacques Fomerand state that the most enduring divide in views of the UN is "the North–South split" between <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_divide_in_the_World" class="mw-redirect" title="North–South divide in the World">richer Northern nations and developing Southern nations</a>. Southern nations tend to favour a more empowered UN with a stronger General Assembly, allowing them a greater voice in world affairs, while Northern nations prefer an economically <a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire">laissez-faire</a> UN that focuses on transnational threats such as terrorism.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009civ&#95;242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009civ-242"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There have been numerous calls for the <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Reform of the United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council's membership to be increased</a>, for different ways of electing the UN's secretary-general, and for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="United Nations Parliamentary Assembly">UN Parliamentary Assembly</a> (UNPA).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Exclusion_of_nations">Exclusion of nations</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_non-self-governing_territories" title="United Nations list of non-self-governing territories">United Nations list of non-self-governing territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">List of states with limited recognition</a></div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Committee_of_National_Liberation" title="French Committee of National Liberation">French Committee of National Liberation</a> was late to be recognized by the United States as the government of France, and so the country was initially excluded from the conferences that created the new organization. Future French president <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> criticized the UN, famously calling it a <i>machin</i> (contraption), and was not convinced that a <a href="/wiki/Global_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Global security">global security</a> alliance would help maintain world peace, preferring <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_France" title="Foreign relations of France">direct defence treaties</a> between countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, the government of China was disputed between the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Chinese Nationalist Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a>. After the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC) on 1 October 1949, the government of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (ROC) retreated to the island of Taiwan,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> continuing to claim that it was the sole government of China. After the civil war, the United Nations continued recognizing the ROC as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_505_(VI)" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 505 (VI)">official government of China</a>. In 1971, amid growing debate over the representation of the Chinese people on the mainland,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the General Assembly passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758_(XXVI)" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758 (XXVI)">a resolution</a> recognizing the PRC as <i>"the only legitimate representatives of China to the United Nations."</i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Critics<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2025)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> allege that this position reflects a failure of the organization's development goals and guidelines,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and it garnered renewed scrutiny during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, when Taiwan was denied membership into the World Health Organization despite its <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Taiwan" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Taiwan">relatively effective response to the virus</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Support for Taiwan's inclusion in the UN remains challenged by the People's Republic of China, which claims the territories controlled by Taiwan <a href="/wiki/One_China" title="One China">as their own territory</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Independence">Independence</h3></div>
<p>Throughout the Cold War, both the United States and the Soviet Union repeatedly accused the UN of favouring the other. In 1950, the Soviet Union boycotted the organization in protest to <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">China's seat at the UN Security Council</a> being given to the anti-communist <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a>. Three years later, the Soviets effectively forced the resignation of UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a> by refusing to acknowledge his administration due to his support of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ironically, the United States had simultaneously scrutinized the UN for employing communists and Soviet sympathizers, following a high-profile accusation that <a href="/wiki/Alger_Hiss" title="Alger Hiss">Alger Hiss</a>, an American who had taken part in the establishment of the UN, had been a Soviet spy. American Senator Joseph McCarthy claimed that the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">UN Secretariat</a> under Secretary-General Lie harboured American communists, leading to further pressure that the UN chief resign.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The United States saw nascent opposition to the UN in the 1960s, particularly amongst conservatives, with groups such as the <a href="/wiki/John_Birch_Society" title="John Birch Society">John Birch Society</a> stating that the organization was an instrument for communism.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Popular opposition to the UN was expressed through bumper stickers and signs with slogans such as "Get the U.S. out of the U.N. and the U.N. out of the U.S.!" and "You can't spell communism without U.N."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199572–73,&#95;82&#95;254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199572–73,_82-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_States_sovereignty">United States sovereignty</h3></div>
<p>In the United States, there were concerns about supposed threats to national sovereignty, most notably promoted by the <a href="/wiki/John_Birch_Society" title="John Birch Society">John Birch Society</a>, which mounted a nationwide campaign in opposition to the UN during the 1960s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in the 1990s, the same concern appeared with the <a href="/wiki/American_Sovereignty_Restoration_Act" title="American Sovereignty Restoration Act">American Sovereignty Restoration Act</a>, which has been introduced multiple times in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>. In 1997, an amendment containing the bill received a floor vote, with 54 representatives voting in favour.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The 2007 version of the bill (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/110th-congress/house-bill/1146">H.R.&#160;1146</a>) was authored by <a href="/wiki/U.S._Representative" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Representative">U.S. Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul" title="Ron Paul">Ron Paul</a>, to effect the United States' withdrawal from the United Nations. It would repeal various laws pertaining to the UN, terminate authorization for funds to be spent on the UN, terminate UN presence on American property, and withdraw diplomatic immunity for UN employees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It would provide up to two years for the United States to withdraw.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lamb&#95;261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lamb-261"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Yale_Law_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Yale Law Journal">Yale Law Journal</a></i> cited the Act as proof that "the United States's complaints against the United Nations have intensified."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The most recent iteration, As of 2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_Nations&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, is H.R.7806, introduced by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rogers_(Alabama_politician)" title="Mike Rogers (Alabama politician)">Mike D. Rogers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>American <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">state lawmakers</a> have proposed legislation to block various UN programs deemed to threaten U.S. sovereignty.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2023, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> enacted legislation to block the implementation of programs "originating in, or traceable to, the United Nations or a subsidiary entity of the United Nations," including <a href="/wiki/Agenda_21" title="Agenda 21">Agenda 21</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">the 2030 Agenda</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Alleged_pro-Palestinian_bias">Alleged pro-Palestinian bias</h3></div>
<p>The UN's attention to Israel's treatment of Palestinians has been considered excessive by Israeli diplomat <a href="/wiki/Dore_Gold" title="Dore Gold">Dore Gold</a> and pro-Israeli individuals and organisations such as British scholar <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._Wistrich" title="Robert S. Wistrich">Robert S. Wistrich</a>, American legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz" title="Alan Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a>, Australian politician <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dreyfus" title="Mark Dreyfus">Mark Dreyfus</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The UNHRC has likewise been accused of anti-Israel bias by Ex-President of the United States <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, who complained that the Council focused too much attention on Israel and not enough on adversaries of the US such as Cuba, Venezuela, North Korea and Iran.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In her confirmation hearing before the Senate panel to be the U.S. ambassador to the United Nations, <a href="/wiki/Elise_Stefanik" title="Elise Stefanik">Elise Stefanik</a>, described the UN's attitude toward Israel as "anti-semitic".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-d827&#95;269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-d827-269"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Effectiveness">Effectiveness</h3></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/Edward_Luck" title="Edward Luck">Edward Luck</a>, the United States has preferred a feeble United Nations in major projects undertaken by the organization to forestall UN interference with, or resistance to, American policies. "The last thing the U.S. wants is an independent UN throwing its weight around", Luck said. Similarly, former <a href="/wiki/US_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="US Ambassador to the United Nations">US Ambassador to the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Patrick_Moynihan" title="Daniel Patrick Moynihan">Daniel Patrick Moynihan</a> explained that "The Department of State desired that the United Nations prove utterly ineffective in whatever measures it undertook. The task was given to me, and I carried it forward with not inconsiderable success."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>269<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, former special representative of the secretary-general of the UN to Somalia <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Sahnoun" title="Mohamed Sahnoun">Mohamed Sahnoun</a> published <i>Somalia: The Missed Opportunities</i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>270<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a book in which he analyses the reasons for the failure of the 1992 UN intervention in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. Sahnoun claims that between the start of the Somali civil war in 1988 and the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> regime in January 1991, the UN missed at least three opportunities to prevent major human tragedies. When the UN tried to provide humanitarian assistance, they were totally outperformed by <a href="/wiki/NGO" class="mw-redirect" title="NGO">NGOs</a>, whose competence and dedication sharply contrasted with the UN's excessive caution and bureaucratic inefficiencies. Sahnoun warned that if radical reform were not undertaken, then the UN would continue to respond to such crises with inept improvisation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>271<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Beyond specific instances or areas of alleged ineffectiveness, some scholars debate the overall effectiveness of the UN. Adherents to the <a href="/wiki/Realism_(international_relations)" title="Realism (international relations)">realist</a> school of international relations take a pessimistic position, arguing that the UN is not an effective organization because it is dominated and constrained by great powers. <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_(international_relations)" title="Liberalism (international relations)">Liberal</a> scholars counter that it is an effective organization because it has proved capable of solving many problems by working around the restrictions imposed by powerful member states. The UN is generally considered by scholars to be more effective in realms such as public health, and humanitarian assistance.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>272<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The ineffectiveness of enforcing <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> in the 21st century<sup id="cite&#95;ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>273<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> have led to debate on possible re-emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_conquest" title="Right of conquest">right of conquest</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Inefficiency_and_corruption">Inefficiency and corruption</h3></div>
<p>Critics have also accused the UN of bureaucratic inefficiency, waste, and corruption. In 1976, the General Assembly established the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Inspection_Unit" title="Joint Inspection Unit">Joint Inspection Unit</a> to seek out inefficiencies within the UN system. During the 1990s, the United States withheld dues citing inefficiency and only started repayment on the condition that a major reforms initiative be introduced. In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_of_Internal_Oversight_Services" title="United Nations Office of Internal Oversight Services">Office of Internal Oversight Services</a> (or the OIOS) was established by the General Assembly to serve as an efficiency watchdog.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, the UN faced accusations that its recently ended <a href="/wiki/Oil-for-Food_Programme" title="Oil-for-Food Programme">Oil-for-Food Programme</a> — in which Iraq had been allowed to trade oil for basic needs to relieve the pressure of sanctions — had suffered from widespread corruption, including billions of dollars of <a href="/wiki/Kickback_(bribery)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kickback (bribery)">kickbacks</a>. An independent inquiry created by the UN found that many of its officials had been involved in <a href="/wiki/Oil-for-Food_Program_Hearings" title="Oil-for-Food Program Hearings">the scheme</a>, and raised significant questions about the role of <a href="/wiki/Kojo_Annan" title="Kojo Annan">Kojo Annan</a>, the son of <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Hymn_to_the_United_Nations">Hymn to the United Nations</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hymn_to_the_United_Nations" title="Hymn to the United Nations">Hymn to the United Nations</a></div>
<p>On the request of then United Nations <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a>, a Hymn to the United Nations was performed on the occasion of its 26th anniversary, on 24 October 1971, by <a href="/wiki/Pau_Casals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pau Casals">Pau Casals</a>, the lyrics to which were penned by the poet <a href="/wiki/W._H._Auden" title="W. H. Auden">W. H. Auden</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>277<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Thant first approached Casals, who was a personal friend, looking to create a hymn to peace and hoping for the song to be based on the preamble of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a>. Thant later commissioned Auden to write the poem after Casals requested one to set to music. <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>Auden completed his work in three days time. The finished work, scored for chorus and orchestra, takes approximately seven minutes to play. However, there were never any plans to adopt the song as the organization's official anthem.
</p>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references" data-mw-group="lower-alpha">
<li id="cite&#95;note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Holy See is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign entity</a> with <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">statehood</a> over the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City State</a>. For details, see <a href="/wiki/Holy_See_and_the_United_Nations" title="Holy See and the United Nations">Holy See and the United Nations</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Poland had not been represented among the fifty nations at the San Francisco conference due to the reluctance of the Western superpowers to recognize its post-war communist government. However, the Charter was later amended to list Poland as a founding member, and Poland ratified the Charter on 16 October 1945.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEGrant200925–26&#95;37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrant200925–26-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some sources identify seventeen specialized agencies, taking into account the three specialized agencies that make up the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>, which is now treated as one organization: the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (IBRD), the <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Association" title="International Development Association">International Development Association</a> (IDA), and the <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a> (IFC).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-142"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-142">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Holy See is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign entity</a> with <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">statehood</a> over the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City State</a>. For details, see <a href="/wiki/Holy_See_and_the_United_Nations" title="Holy See and the United Nations">Holy See and the United Nations</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
